            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultrafine SnS2 nanocrystals-reduced graphene oxide nanoribbon paper (SnS2-RGONRP) was created by a well-designed process including in situ redn., evapn.-induced self-assembly, and sulfuration.  The as-formed SnS2 nanocrystals possess an av. diam. of 2.3 nm and disperse on the surface of RGONRs uniformly.  The strong capillary force formed during evapn. leads to a compact assembly of RGONRs to give a flexible paper structure with a high d. of 0.94 g/cm3.  The as-prepd. SnS2-RGONRP composite could be directly used as free-standing electrode for Na ion batteries.  Due to the synergistic effects between the ultrafine SnS2 nanocrystals and the conductive, tightly connected RGONR networks, the composite paper electrode exhibits excellent electrochem. performance.  A high volumetric capacity of 508-244 mAh/cm3 was obtained at current densities of 0.1-10 A/g.  Discharge capacities of 334 and 255 mAh/cm3 were still kept, even after 1500 cycles tested at current densities of 1 and 5 A/g, resp.  This strategy provides insight into a new pathway for the creation of free-standing composite electrodes used in the energy storage and conversion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoCYhQE_YL7F7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljgqLP8ztLcNg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXmsFWku7Y%253D&amp;md5=75201ed26dc4be08a6c0cdb3ad070998</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201304962"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Engelhard, M.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Probing the Failure Mechanism of SnO2 Nanowires for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gu, Meng; Kushima, Akihiro; Shao, Yuyan; Zhang, Ji-Guang; Liu, Jun; Browning, Nigel D.; Li, Ju; Wang, Chongmin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Non-lithium metals such as Na have attracted attention as a potential charge carrying ion for rechargeable batteries.  Using in situ TEM in combination with d. functional theory calcns., the authors probed the structural and chem. evolution of SnO2 nanowire anodes in Na-ion batteries and compared them quant. with results from Li-ion batteries.  Upon Na insertion into SnO2, a displacement reaction occurs, giving amorphous NaxSn nanoparticles dispersed in Na2O matrix.  With further Na insertion, the NaxSn crystd. into Na15Sn4 (x = 3.75).  Upon extn. of Na (de-sodiation), the NaxSn transforms to Sn nanoparticles.  Assocd. with the de-alloying, pores form, leading to a structure of Sn particles confined in a hollow matrix of Na2O.  These pores greatly increase elec. impedance, therefore accounting for the poor cyclability of SnO2.  DFT calcns. indicate that Na+ diffuses 30 times slower than Li+ in SnO2, in agreement with in situ TEM measurement.  Insertion of Na can chemomechanically soften the reaction product to a greater extent than in lithiation.  Therefore, in contrast to the lithiation of SnO2 significantly less dislocation plasticity was seen ahead of the sodiation front.  This direct comparison of the results from Na and Li highlights the crit. role of ionic size and electronic structure of different ionic species on the charge/discharge rate and failure mechanisms in these batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrxbnVD4FT9W7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljgqLP8ztLcNg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsFels7zP&amp;md5=3eeb24d9885b1c825918e689b7adbbb2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-014-0506-z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Seng, K.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">SnSb@carbon nanocable anchored on graphene sheets for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Li; Seng, Kuok Hau; Li, Dan; Xia, Yongyao; Liu, Hua Kun; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1466-1476</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NRAEB5</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The development of materials with unique nanostructures is an effective strategy for the improvement of sodium storage in sodium ion batteries to achieve stable cycling performance and good rate capability.  In this work, SnSb core/carbon-shell nanocables directly anchored on graphene sheets (GS) were synthesized by the hydrothermal technique and chem. vapor deposition.  The simultaneous carbon coating and the encapsulation of SnSb alloy is effective for alleviating the vol.-change problem in sodium ion batteries.  After optimizing the electrolyte for SnSb in the sodium ion batteries, the optimized coaxial SnSb/carbon nanocable/GS (SnSb/CNT@GS) nanostructure demonstrated stable cycling capability and rate performance in 1 M NaClO4 with propylene carbonate (PC) + 5% fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC).  The SnSb/CNT@GS electrode can retain a capacity of 360 mAh/g for up to 100 cycles, which is 71% of the theor. capacity.  This is higher than in the other three electrolytes tested (1 M NaClO4 in PC, 1 M NaClO4 in PC/FEC (1:1 vol./vol.) and 1 M NaPF6 + PC), and higher than that of the sample without the addn. of graphene.  The good electrochem. performance can be attributed to the efficient buffering provided by the outer carbon nanocable layer and the graphene inhibiting the agglomeration of SnSb particles, as well as its high cond.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpxy6wY3P3PGrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljgqLP8ztLcNg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtlKht7nF&amp;md5=831cecb3ad9e9fd6b40bfcb18ffc4a15</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA01963J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jahel, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ghimbeu, C.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exceptionally highly performing Na-ion battery anode using crystalline SnO2 nanoparticles confined in mesoporous carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jahel, Ali; Ghimbeu, Camelia Matei; Darwiche, Ali; Vidal, Loic; Hajjar-Garreau, Samar; Vix-Guterl, Cathie; Monconduit, Laure</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11960-11969</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Confined and unconfined SnO2 nanoparticles in the pores of mesoporous carbon were prepd. and tested as anode materials vs. Na.  Both composites present small cryst. SnO2 particles (∼3 nm) but different location and dispersion in the carbon matrix.  When the particles are homogeneously distributed and confined in the carbon pores, an initial reversible capacity of 780 mA h g-1 is achieved with unprecedented capacity retention of 80 and 54% after 100 and 4000 cycles, resp., at a high current rate (50 C, 1800 mA g-1).  Unexpectedly, over two current rate variation cycles from 1 C to 500 C, the composite recovers 81% and 97%, resp. after returning from the 500 C to the 1 C rate.  To our knowledge, no other material with such a long cycling life and superior performance in terms of capacity and rate capability has been reported so far for sodium ion batteries.  HRTEM, XRD, N2 adsorption, XPS and galvanostatic cycling results suggest that confined SnO2 particles undergo an enhanced sodium alloying/dealloying process due to their special confinement inside the pores, which increases their cond., facilitates the diffusion of Na+ ions and buffers the large volumetric changes during charge/discharge.  These high performances cannot be delivered when SnO2 is not confined and not well dispersed in the carbon pores.  This work demonstrates that nano-confinement of anode species in carbon is a valuable concept affording the modification of the fundamental properties of guest species along with their electrochem. performances leading to highly stable and performing materials with a long life for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpmSgtWPTSt8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljgqLP8ztLcNg"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion Battery is attractive alternative to Li-ion battery due to the natural abundance of Na resource.  Searching for suitable anode materials is one of the crit. issues for Na-ion battery due to the low Na-storage activity of C materials.  The authors synthesized a nanohybrid anode consisting of ultrafine SnO2 anchored on few-layered reduced graphene oxide (rGO) by a facile hydrothermal route.  The SnO2/rGO hybrid exhibits a high capacity, long cycle life and good rate capability.  The hybrid can deliver a high charge capacity of 324 mAh g-1SnO2 at 50 mA g-1.  At 1600 mA g-1 (2.4 C), it can still yield a charge capacity of 200 mAh g-1SnO2.  After 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1, the hybrid can retain a high charge capacity of 369 mAh g-1SnO2.  XPS, ex situ TEM and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy were used to study the origin of the excellent electrochem. Na-storage properties of SnO2/rGO.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrL1XmUDBLGurVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhIK7xOv06NZg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVyhs7zN&amp;md5=cffea851d27feb1ad7ee9852fec28296</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1016/j.matlet.2016.09.089"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ren, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ding, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Three-dimensional SnS<sub>2</sub> Flowers/Carbon Nanotubes Network: Extraordinary Rate Capacity for Sodium-ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Mater.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile 1-step hydrothermal route was developed to prep. SnS2/reduced graphene oxide nanocomposites (TSG) with hexagonal SnS2 nanoplates and ultrafine nanocrystals grown and distributed uniformly on the graphene nanosheets. Li-ion storage performance of the TSG nanocomposites was studied by using cyclic voltammetry, galvanostatic charge-discharge, and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy.  The TSG electrode exhibited exceptional high reversible capacity with good cycling stability (1005 mAh g-1 after 200 cycles at the c.d. of 100 mA g-1), and extraordinary rate capability (612 mAh g-1 at the rate of 2000 mA g-1).  The superior performance could be attributed to the large available surface area, high cond. and fast transportation of electrons and Li ions, which were benefited from the unique structure of the material and the synergistic effect between SnS2 and graphene.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoP-zOhrP6yTbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhIK7xOv06NZg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtVyrsLk%253D&amp;md5=686929fd160896c7b86ded83d3425c74</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2016.12.215"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yin, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chai, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ma, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kong, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bai, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effects of Binders on Electrochemical Properties of the SnS<sub>2</sub> Nanostructured Anode of the Lithium-ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effects of binders on electrochemical properties of the SnS2 nanostructured anode of the lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Lixiong; Chai, Simin; Ma, Jianzhong; Huang, Jianfeng; Kong, Xingang; Bai, Peijie; Liu, Yao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">698</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">828-834</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JALCEU</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Binders play a significant role in enhancing the electrochem. performance of tin disulfide (SnS2) as the anode for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) because of their excellent dispersion and cohesion in the electrodes.  In the present work, flake-like SnS2 nanoparticles with a hexagonal structure were synthesized by a facile one-step hydrothermal method with a mean grain size of 7.7 nm.  When sodium alginate (SA), CM-cellulose (CMC), poly acrylic acid (PAA), and CMC-PAA (1:1, wt%) are applied as binders for the SnS2 anode electrode (the obtained electrodes are denoted as SnS2-S, SnS2-C, SnS2-CP, and SnS2-P, resp.) in LIBs, the electrodes exhibited high reversible lithium-ion storage capacities of 762.00 mA h g-1, 891.65 mA h g-1, 913.94 mA h g-1, and 930.36 mA h g-1 at the current densities of 100 mA g-1, resp.  Importantly, the SnS2-P electrode exhibited excellent rate capacity and cycling performance.  The -COOH of PAA attached to SnS2 can increase the amt. of free radicals, which can prevent the detachment of SnS2 from the current collector, and the carboxyl group can effectively inhibit the vol. expansion and pulverization of particles of the electrode.  Undoubtedly, PAA binder significantly improves the cycling and rate performances of SnS2 anode material for LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpV6pZSLdIF7LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgPsY_vWNlP5Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhs1KhsA%253D%253D&amp;md5=bdb3d956af782b2982330e367b57839d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1039/c3ta11269a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mei, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ma, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Superior Electrochemical Performance of Ultrasmall SnS<sub>2</sub> Nanocrystals Decorated on Flexible RGO in Lithium-ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Superior electrochemical performance of ultrasmall SnS2 nanocrystals decorated on flexible RGO in lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mei, Lin; Xu, Cheng; Yang, Ting; Ma, Jianmin; Chen, Libao; Li, Qiuhong; Wang, Taihong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">30</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A hybrid structure involving efficient plentiful ultrasmall SnS2 nanocrystals decorated on flexible reduced graphene oxide (RGO) has been successfully realized via a simple refluxing method.  Compared to previous studies, the ultrasmall SnS2 nanocrystals can compactly and orderly cover the RGO nanosheets, increasing the loading no. of SnS2 per unit area of the RGO substrates.  The ultrasmall SnS2 nanocrystals@RGO nanocomposites were investigated as electrode materials for lithium-ion batteries.  In this hybrid structure, RGO was not only used as a solid support to uniformly distribute the SnS2 nanocrystals, but also as a carrier to accelerate electron transport.  In addn., the uniform size and homogeneous SnS2 nanocrystals on the RGO nanosheets reduced electrode polarization, resulting in excellent electrochem. performance for lithium-ion batteries.  A specific capacity up to 1034 mA-h/g was realized from an ultrasmall SnS2 nanocrystals@RGO electrode even after 200 cycles at 0.1C.  Importantly, the ultrasmall SnS2 nanocrystals@RGO electrode showed excellent capacity retention for up to 450 cycles even at a high rate of 5C.  The cost-effective synthesis of SnS2 nanocrystals@RGO and excellent electrochem. performance indicates the great potential for this type of nanocomposites as an active electrode for lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrXs8TIer8ZtLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgPsY_vWNlP5Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtVyjurrM&amp;md5=6142fd575360f710a7f3045eb5398e8a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201402833"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Few-layered SnS<sub>2</sub> on Few-layered Reduced Graphene Oxide as Na-ion Battery Anode with Ultralong Cycle Life and Superior Rate Capability</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv. Funct.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Few-Layered SnS2 on Few-Layered Reduced Graphene Oxide as Na-Ion Battery Anode with Ultralong Cycle Life and Superior Rate Capability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yandong; Zhu, Peiyi; Huang, Liliang; Xie, Jian; Zhang, Shichao; Cao, Gaoshao; Zhao, Xinbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have been considered as promising alternatives to Li-ion batteries due to the natural abundance of sodium resources.  Searching for high-performance anode materials currently becomes a hot topic and also a great challenge for developing Na-ion batteries.  In this work, a novel hybrid anode is synthesized consisting of ultrafine, few-layered SnS2 anchored on few-layered reduced graphene oxide (rGO) by a facile solvothermal route.  The SnS2/rGO hybrid exhibits a high capacity, ultralong cycle life, and superior rate capability.  The hybrid can deliver a high charge capacity of 649 mA-h/g at 100 mA/g. The hybrid can also sustain a c.d. up to 12.8 A/g (≈28C) where the charge process can be completed in only 1.3 min while still delivering a charge capacity of 337 mA-h/g.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exfoliated-SnS2 restacked on graphene as a high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Kang, Hongyan; Jiao, Lifang; Chen, Chengcheng; Cao, Kangzhe; Wang, Yijing; Yuan, Huatang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Designed as a high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life anode for sodium ion batteries, exfoliated-SnS2 restacked on graphene is prepd. by the hydrolysis of lithiated SnS2 followed by a facile hydrothermal method.  Structural and morphol. characterizations demonstrate that ultrasmall SnS2 nanoplates (with a typical size of 20-50 nm) composed of 2-5 layers are homogeneously decorated on the surface of graphene, while the hybrid structure self-assembles into a three-dimensional (3D) network architecture. More impressively, the capacity can reach 326 mA h g-1 even at 4000 mA g-1 and remains stable at ∼610 mA h g-1 without fading up to 300 cycles when the rate is brought back to 200 mA g-1.  The excellent electrochem. performance is attributed to the synergetic effects between the ultrasmall SnS2 and the highly conductive graphene network.  The unique structure can simultaneously facilitate Na+ ion diffusion, provide more reaction sites, and suppress aggregation and vol. fluctuation of the active materials during prolonged cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRwuFHeQ2-ZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgPsY_vWNlP5Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhslelt7fN&amp;md5=8bd01685b22c4afe0f313378ef72187b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1039/c2cp40790f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xin, H.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Doping carbons beyond nitrogen: an overview of advanced heteroatom doped carbons with boron, sulphur and phosphorus for energy applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Paraknowitsch, Jens Peter; Thomas, Arne</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2839-2855</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Heteroatom doped carbon materials represent one of the most prominent families of materials that are used in energy related applications, such as fuel cells, batteries, hydrogen storage or supercapacitors.  While doping carbons with nitrogen atoms has experienced great progress throughout the past decades and yielded promising material concepts, also other doping candidates have gained the researchers' interest in the last few years.  Boron is already relatively widely studied, and as its electronic situation is contrary to the one of nitrogen, codoping carbons with both heteroatoms can probably create synergistic effects.  Sulfur and phosphorus have just recently entered the world of carbon synthesis, but already the first studies published prove their potential, esp. as electrocatalysts in the cathodic compartment of fuel cells.  Due to their size and their electronegativity being lower than those of carbon, structural distortions and changes of the charge densities are induced in the carbon materials.  This article is to give a state of the art update on the most recent developments concerning the advanced heteroatom doping of carbon that goes beyond nitrogen.  Doped carbon materials and their applications in energy devices are discussed with respect to their boron-, sulfur- and phosphorus-doping.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrXYE3FbkNibrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgPsY_vWNlP5Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsV2it7fO&amp;md5=182291f9157be822fc6701fac47f4c00</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201405370"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wickramaratne, N.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Integrated 3D porous C-MoS2/nitrogen-doped graphene electrode for high capacity and prolonged stability lithium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie, D.; Tang, W. J.; Xia, X. H.; Wang, D. H.; Zhou, D.; Shi, F.; Wang, X. L.; Gu, C. D.; Tu, J. P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">296</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">392-399</span>CODEN:

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Scrupulous design and fabrication of advanced anode materials are of great importance for developing high-performance lithium ion batteries.  Herein, we report a facile strategy for construction of free-standing and free-binder 3D porous carbon coated MoS2/nitrogen-doped graphene (C-MoS2/N-G) integrated electrode via a hydrothermal-induced self-assembly process.  The preformed carbon coated MoS2 is strongly anchored on the porous nitrogen-doped graphene aerogel architecture.  As an anode for lithium ion batteries, the C-MoS2/N-G electrode delivers a high first discharge capacity of 1600 mAh g-1 and maintains 900 mAh g-1 after 500 cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1.  Impressively, superior high-rate capability is achieved for the C-MoS2/N-G with a reversible capacity of 500 mAh g-1 at a high c.d. of 4000 mA g-1.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen and sulfur dual-doped graphene sheets as anode materials with superior cycling stability for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Yuqi; Zeng, Yan; Xu, Dandan; Li, Peihang; Wang, Heng-guo; Li, Xiang; Li, Yanhui; Wang, Yinghui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Novel N and S dual-doped graphene sheets were synthesized via carbonization of poly(2,5-dimercapto-1,3,4-thiadiazole) (PDMcT) functionalized graphene oxides.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sulfur/Nitrogen Dual-doped Porous Graphene Aerogels Enhancing Anode Performance of Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shan, Hui; Li, Xifei; Cui, Yanhua; Xiong, Dongbin; Yan, Bo; Li, Dejun; Lushington, Andrew; Sun, Xueliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">S/N dual-doped graphene aerogels (SNGAs) with a unique porous network structure were designed through a facile and versatile 1-pot hydrothermal strategy.  When employed as anode in LIBs, the SNGAs with N content of 1.50% and S content of 15.11% exhibit superior cycle life and rate capability.  For example, a high reversible capacity of 1109.8 mAh g-1 can be obtained after 400 cycles even at a high c.d. of 800 mA g-1.  It was discreetly demonstrated that the prominent improved performance of SNGAs can be mainly ascribed to the effect of dual-doping heteroatoms in cooperation with each other in to the graphene lattice as well as the porous nanostructure facilitating the mass transfer for both ions and electrons.  The authors' conclusions illustrate that the strategy of dual-doped graphene aerogel may promote the potential application of graphene for high performance Li ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqx8YbO2cWnRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lga4o-dYsID7w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XntVGhtro%253D&amp;md5=8a021fd5255ef4127a3b2480786cf9b1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1039/c3nr04823c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lushington, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structurally Tailored Graphene Nanosheets as Lithium Ion Battery Anodes: An Insight to Yield Exceptionally High Lithium Storage Performance</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">12607</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">12615</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structurally tailored graphene nanosheets as lithium ion battery anodes: an insight to yield exceptionally high lithium storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Xifei; Hu, Yuhai; Liu, Jian; Lushington, Andrew; Li, Ruying; Sun, Xueliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">How to tune graphene nanosheets (GNSs) with various morphologies has been a significant challenge for lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  In this study, three types of GNSs with varying size, edge sites, defects and layer nos. have been successfully achieved.  It was demonstrated that controlling GNS morphol. and microstructure has important effects on its cyclic performance and rate capability in LIBs.  Diminished GNS layer no., decreased size, increased edge sites and increased defects in the GNS anode can be highly beneficial to lithium storage and result in increased electrochem. performance.  Interestingly, GNSs treated with a hydrothermal approach delivered a high reversible discharge capacity of 1348 mA h g-1.  This study demonstrates that the controlled design of high performance GNS anodes is an important concept in LIB applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr5ali9odG2K7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhMtghm4NkTKQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvVejurrE&amp;md5=1d83b24f9f1c1ec31163deddbf6ede55</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1021/ja01539a017"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hummers, W.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable sodium-ion batteries have lately received considerable attention as an alternative to lithium-ion batteries because sodium resources are essentially inexhaustible and ubiquitous around the world.  Despite recent reports on cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries have shown electrochem. activities close to their lithium-ion counterparts, the major scientific challenge for sodium-ion batteries is to exploit efficient anode materials.  Herein, we demonstrate that a hybrid material composed of few-layer SnS2 nanosheets sandwiched between reduced graphene oxide (RGO) nanosheets exhibits a high specific capacity of 843 mAh/g (calcd. based on the mass of SnS2 only) at a c.d. of 0.1 A/g and a 98% capacity retention after 100 cycles when evaluated between 0.01 and 2.5 V.  Employing ex situ high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy and selected area electron diffraction techniques, we illustrate the high specific capacity of our anode through a 3-fold mechanism of intercalation of sodium ions along the ab-plane of SnS2 nanosheets and the subsequent formation of Na2S2 and Na15Sn4 through conversion and alloy reactions.  The existence of RGO nanosheets in the hybrid material functions as a flexible backbone and high-speed electronic pathways, guaranteeing that an appropriate resilient space buffers the anisotropic dilation of SnS2 nanosheets along the ab-plane and c-axis for stable cycling performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp7u2__bTlgVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhMtghm4NkTKQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXitVCjtrg%253D&amp;md5=8512fccffb30789680f4d2b2a62843db</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1021/am302124f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Preferentialc-axis Orientation of Ultrathin SnS<sub>2</sub> Nanoplates on Graphene as High-performance Anode for Li-ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two dimensional graphene-SnS2 hybrids with superior rate capability for lithium ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Bin; Fang, Yan; Wang, Bin; Zhou, Jisheng; Song, Huaihe; Zhi, Linjie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel porous nanoarchitecture composed of 2D graphene-SnS2 (G-SnS2) units is developed via a two-step approach in this work.  The special structure endows the high-rate transportation of electrolyte ions and electrons throughout the electrode matrix, resulting in remarkable electrochem. performance when it was used as anode in lithium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrF2M0sjYQszbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhMtghm4NkTKQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhs1CgsbvI&amp;md5=73e2d25e08ff9713e3c0257b3e2528b4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1021/jp108864y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Banis, M.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen Doping Effects on Carbon Nanotubes and the Origin of the Enhanced Electrocatalytic Activity of Supported Pt for Proton-Exchange Membrane Fuel Cells</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Yougui; Wang, Jiajun; Liu, Hao; Banis, Mohammad Norouzi; Li, Ruying; Sun, Xueliang; Sham, Tsun-Kong; Ye, Siyu; Knights, Shanna</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">115</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3769-3776</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1932-7447</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon nanotubes (CNTs) and nitrogen-doped carbon nanotubes (CNx) were synthesized by the floating catalyst CVD (FCCVD) method.  Pt nanoparticles were deposited onto the two catalyst supports with the ethylene glycol redn. method.  Different from CNTs that contain straight hollow tubes, CNx contain a bamboolike structure with kinks along the tubes and more surface defects.  XPS confirms the nitrogen atoms in the graphite matrix and reveals the chem. natures of the doped nitrogen atoms.  Carbon K-edge near-edge x-ray absorption fine structure (NEXAFS) and Raman characterizations reveal higher defective quantity in CNx than CNTs.  The unique structure and surface property of CNx leads to a better dispersion of Pt nanoparticles on CNx than on CNTs, as revealed by TEM images.  Pt supported on CNx (Pt/CNx) exhibited a higher electrochem. surface area (ECSA) and higher catalytic activity toward oxygen redn. reaction (ORR), in comparison to Pt supported on CNTs (Pt/CNTs).  Better performance of Pt/CNx than Pt/CNTs was confirmed by single-cell fuel cell tests.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpKBa1zh9q66LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgdXccVAuqtSg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhvFWit7Y%253D&amp;md5=3d534771fa41bb1338d6df366595f360</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1021/am301962d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flexible Free-standing Graphene/SnO(2) Nanocomposites Paper for Li-ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-dimensional structure-based tin disulfide/vertically aligned carbon nanotube arrays composites as high-performance anode materials for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Deng, Weina; Chen, Xiaohua; Liu, Zheng; Hu, Aiping; Tang, Qunli; Li, Zhe; Xiong, Yina</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">277</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">131-138</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Three-dimensional structure-based tin disulfide/vertically aligned carbon nanotube arrays (VACNTs) composites have been successfully fabricated by a facile hydrothermal method for self-assembly with the help of nebulization-assisted infiltration.  The SnS2 particles are anchored on the surface of the VACNTs and the no. of these nanoparticles increases as the nebulization time increase.  The novel three-dimensional structure-based SnS2/VACNTs sample with the SnS2 content of 67 wt.% exhibits excellent electrochem. performance, including high capacity (738 mA-h/g at 50 mA/g after 1st cycle), good cycle stability (551 mA-h/g at 100 mA/g after 100 cycles), and excellent rate capability (223 mA-h/g at 2000 mA/g) when used as an anode in lithium-ion batteries.  The high electrochem. performance can be attributed to the synergistic effect of SnS2 and the unique microstructure of VACNTs, which provide the rapid pathways for ionic and electronic transport ascribing to their well-directed one-dimensional conductive electron paths and well defined regular pore structures.  The VACNTs serve as not only conductive additives to improve the cond. of SnS2 in the composites, but also as buffer matrix to restrain the vol. change of SnS2 and stabilize the electrode structure during the alloying/dealloying process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqOvZz-WSH4CrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgdXccVAuqtSg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitVakt7nL&amp;md5=0df0414ed7a1fac249de5ea8ec21c1b9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.03.048"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shen, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In Situ Assembly of Graphene Sheets-supported SnS<sub>2</sub> Nanoplates into 3D Macroporous Aerogels for High-performance Lithium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ assembly of graphene sheets-supported SnS2 nanoplates into 3D macroporous aerogels for high-performance lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jiang, Xin; Yang, Xiaoling; Zhu, Yihua; Shen, Jianhua; Fan, Kaicai; Li, Chunzhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Three-dimensional (3D) SnS2/graphene aerogels (SnS2/G-As) have been successfully fabricated via an in situ macroscopy self-assembly of graphene sheets which embedded SnS2 nanoplates in a hydrothermal process, and then freeze-drying to maintain the 3D monolithic architectures.  The graphene sheets in high concn. will be easily restacked into 3D architectures driven by combined hydrophobic and π-π stacking interactions during hydrothermal redn. process, meanwhile SnS2 facilitate stabilizing such novel graphene networks.  The obtained SnS2/G-As show interconnected graphene networks, large surface area and large nos. of macropores.  The novel 3D architectures in SnS2/G-As, which can provide rich sites for absorbing lithium ions and facilitate electrolyte contact as well as ionic diffusion, combined with the synergistic effect between the layered SnS2 and the graphene make SnS2/G-As achieve high reversible capacity (656 mA h g-1 with a coulombic efficiency of over 95% after 30 cycles) and excellent rate capability (240 mA h g-1 at the rate of 1000 mA g-1) when used as an anode in rechargeable LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGroUldJAMvwNLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgdXccVAuqtSg"> &gt;&gt; The resultant amorphous carbon is endowed with the integrated advantage of featuring high reversible capacity and long cycling stability: intrinsic doping of sulfur, large specific area, and broad mesopore size distribution.  Electrochem. evaluation shows that the SMAC electrode exhibits highly enhanced electrochem. performances, compared with the electrode of non-doped mesoporous and amorphous carbon prepd. by using a different surfactant (sodium laurate).                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly ordered nitrogen-rich mesoporous carbon derived from biomass waste for high-performance lithium-sulfur batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qu, Yaohui; Zhang, Zhian; Zhang, Xiahui; Ren, Guodong; Lai, Yanqing; Liu, Yexiang; Li, Jie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel highly ordered nitrogen-rich mesoporous carbon (HNMC) was prepd. by pyrolysis of biomass waste (gelatin) and a simple template process, and sulfur-HNMC composite based on HNMC was synthesized for lithium-sulfur batteries by a melt-diffusion method.  The elemental sulfur was homogeneously dispersed inside the meso-pores of HNMC based on the analyses.  Electrochem. tests reveal that the sulfur-HNMC (53.3% sulfur) composite shows high rate capability and long cycling stability as cathode materials.  The sulfur-HNMC (53.3% sulfur) composite cathode exhibits a high initial discharge capacity of 1209 mAh g-1 and retains ≤600 mAh g-1 after 200 cycles at 1 C.  Also, the cathode also presents a long term cycling stability up to 300 cycles even at 3 C.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineering SnS2 nanosheet assemblies for enhanced electrochemical lithium and sodium ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yeyun; Zhou, Junhua; Wu, Jinghua; Chen, Fengjiao; Li, Peirong; Han, Na; Huang, Wenjing; Liu, Yuping; Ye, Hualin; Zhao, Feipeng; Li, Yanguang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The reversible electrochem. storage of Li+ and Na+ ions is the operating basis of secondary Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  In recent years, there has been rapid growth in the search for appropriate electrode materials.  Nevertheless, the development of host materials for active and durable electrochem. storage of both Li+ and Na+ ions remain challenging.  We report a facile solvothermal method to prep. hierarchical assemblies of thin SnS2 nanosheets in N-methyl-2-pyrrolidone.  The as-prepd. product has an expanded layered structure due to the presence of org. intercalates.  Mild annealing restores the normal 2H-SnS2 phase with the hierarchical architecture preserved. It was further coated with a thin C layer as the phys. and elec. reinforcement, which led to a much improved cycle life at both low and high current rates.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rapidly Synthesized, Few-Layered Pseudocapacitive SnS2 Anode for High-Power Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Thangavel, Ranjith; Samuthira Pandian, Amaresh; Ramasamy, Hari Vignesh; Lee, Yun-Sung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">46</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">40187-40196</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The abundance of sodium resources has recently motivated the investigation of sodium ion batteries (SIBs) as an alternative to com. lithium ion batteries.  However, the low power and low capacity of conventional sodium anodes hinder their practical realization.  Although most research has concd. on the development of high-capacity sodium anodes, anodes with a combination of high power and high capacity have not been widely realized.  Herein, we present a simple microwave irradn. technique for obtaining few-layered, ultrathin two-dimensional SnS2 over graphene sheets in a few minutes.  SnS2 possesses a large no. of active surface sites and exhibits high-capacity, rapid sodium ion storage kinetics induced by quick, nondestructive pseudocapacitance.  Enhanced sodium ion storage at a high c.d. (12 A g-1), accompanied by high reversibility and high stability, was demonstrated.  Addnl., a rationally designed sodium ion full cell coupled with SnS2//Na3V2(PO4)3 exhibited exceptional performance with high initial Coulombic efficiency (99%), high capacity, high stability, and a retention of ∼53% of the initial capacity even after the c.d. was increased by a factor of 140.  In addn., a high specific energy of ∼140 Wh kg-1 and an ultrahigh specific power of ∼8.3 kW kg-1 (based on the mass of both the anode and cathode) were obsd.  Because of its outstanding performance and rapid synthesis, few-layered SnS2 could be a promising candidate for practical realization of high-power SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrGRiDOPGxr67Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhjmcW3z70HoQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhslags77F&amp;md5=b0d6b6a8322c73803b08e14a8891aae0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1039/c3ta15248k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Prikhodchenko, P.                         cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">SnS2 Nanowall Arrays toward High-Performance Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Peng; Wang, Xiao; Guan, Wenhao; Zhang, Dan; Fang, Libin; Jiang, Yinzhu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cost-effective sodium ion batteries (SIBs) are emerging as a desirable alternative choice to lithium ion batteries in terms of application in large-scale energy storage devices.  SnS2 is regarded as a potential anode material for SIBs because of its unique layered structure and high theor. specific capacity.  However, the development of SnS2 was hindered by the sluggish kinetics of the diffusion process and the inevitable vol. change during repeated sodiation- desodiation processes.  In this work, SnS2 with a unique nanowall array (NWA) structure is fabricated by one-step pulsed spray evapn. chem. vapor deposition (PSE-CVD), which could be used directly as binder-free and carbon-free anodes for SIBs.  The SnS2 NWA electrode achieves a high reversible capacity of 576 mAh g-1 at 500 mA g-1 and enhanced cycling stability.  Attractively, an excellent rate capability is demonstrated with ∼370 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1, corresponding to a capacity retention of 64.2% at 500 mA g-1.  The superior sodium storage capability of the SnS2 NWA electrode could be attributed to outstanding electrode design and a rational growth process, which favor fast electron and Na-ion transport, as well as provide steady structure for elongated cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpGXtGr2cKfFrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhjmcW3z70HoQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXht1eiurg%253D&amp;md5=e9231a5ee5bb3602d5873564a8cd8230</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b02413"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mao, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gao, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mignerey, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Solid-state Fabrication of SnS<sub>2</sub>/C Nanospheres for High-performance Sodium Ion Battery Anode</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solid-State Fabrication of SnS2/C Nanospheres for High-Performance Sodium Ion Battery Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jingjing; Luo, Chao; Mao, Jianfeng; Zhu, Yujie; Fan, Xiulin; Gao, Tao; Mignerey, Alice C.; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin disulfide (SnS2) has emerged as a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries (NIBs) due to its unique layered structure, high theor. capacity, and low cost.  Conventional SnS2 nanomaterials are normally synthesized using hydrothermal method, which is time-consuming and difficult to scale up for mass prodn.  In this study, we develop a simple solid-state reaction method, in which the carbon-coated SnS2 (SnS2/C) anode materials were synthesized by annealing metallic Sn, sulfur powder, and polyacrylonitrile in a sealed vacuum glass tube.  The SnS2/C nanospheres with unique layered structure exhibit a high reversible capacity of 660 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 50 mA g-1 and maintain at 570 mAh g-1 for 100 cycles with a degrdn. rate of 0.14% per cycle, demonstrating one of the best cycling performances in all reported SnS2/C anodes for NIBs to date.  The superior cycling stability of SnS2/C electrode is attributed to the stable nanosphere morphol. and structural integrity during charge/discharge cycles as evidenced by ex situ characterization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoWDnHlGxRZbLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhjmcW3z70HoQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Controlled growth of flower-like SnS2 hierarchical structures with superior performance for lithium-ion battery applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Wenbin; Yang, Youwen; Ma, Dongming; Wang, Hui; Zhang, Yong; Hu, Hanyun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Ionics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">21</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Controlled growth of flower-like SnS2 hierarchical structures was obtained by a facile hydrothermal method with the mixt. soln. of SnCl4 and L-cysteine (L-cys).  The results of electron microscopy and X-ray diffraction characterization indicated that morphol., structure, and crystallinity of the hierarchical structures were seriously dependent on the concn. of L-cys, mole ratio of Sn4+ to L-cys and temp. Acta</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">242</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">117</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">124</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2017.05.023</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D242%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D117-124%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DD.%2BGuan%26author%3DL.%2BMa%26author%3DD.%2BPan%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DX.%2BGao%26author%3DY.%2BXie%26author%3DM.%2BQiu%26author%3DC.%2BYuan%26title%3DAtomic%2BLayer%2BDeposition%2Bof%2BAlumina%2BCoatings%2Bonto%2BSnS2%2Bfor%2BLithium-ion%2BBattery%2BApplications%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2017.05.023&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b18195&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2017.05.023&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atomic Layer Deposition of Alumina Coatings onto SnS2 for Lithium-Ion Battery Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guan, Dongsheng; Ma, Lulu; Pan, Dongqing; Li, Jianyang; Gao, Xianfeng; Xie, Yuanyuan; Qiu, Ming; Yuan, Chris</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">242</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">117-124</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sn disulfide (SnS2) hierarchical structures were synthesized via a simple hydrothermal route for their use in Li-ion batteries.  The issue of fast capacity degrdn. over cycling because of the dramatic vol. change that causes particle pulverization and poor contact between the active material and current collector is explored and alleviated for the 1st time by surface modification of the whole SnS2 electrode via a facile at. layer deposition (ALD).  ALD allows the uniform formation of conformal Al2O3 coatings onto the porous electrode, and thereby succeeds to enhance their electrochem. performance.  As compared, within fifty battery cycles the bare SnS2 electrode exhibits a final capacity of 219.2 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1, while the coated electrode can deliver the final capacity of 351.1 mA h g-1 (60% larger).  The capacity retention and rate capability of the coated electrode is found much better than that of the bare one.  Electrochem. impedance spectroscopy analyses indicate that the resistance derived from solid-electrolyte interface (SEI) and charge transfer process remains fairly smaller in the coated electrode than in the bare one.  The better electrode kinetics accounts for the strengthened Li-ion intercalation behaviors of the modified electrodes, and demonstrates that ALD oxide coatings are able to enhance the mech. integrity and structural stability of SnS2 electrodes, thus effectively impeding the pulverization of active particles and maintaining good electronic conduction paths and efficient charge transfer.  Also, ALD coatings cover the entire electrode and reduce electrolyte decompn. to attenuate the SEI layer, which also contributes to the cyclability of SnS2.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq6i2Kw6kYT8bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liRwM_OUwQkjA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXnslOmsbk%253D&amp;md5=f4407448c59c143fcec4462e76a86414</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref57'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit57" data-doi="10.1021/am200933m"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhai, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Du, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Multiwalled Carbon Nanotubes Anchored with SnS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets as High-performance Anode Materials of Lithium-ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl. As a cathode material, Na3V2(PO4)3/C exhibited an initial specific discharge capacity of 98.17 mA-h/g at 0.1C for potentials ranging from 2.5 to 3.8 V. As an anode material, Na3V2(PO4)3/C exhibited an initial specific discharge capacity of 63.2 mA-h/g at 0.1C for potentials ranging from 1.0 to 2.5 V.  This was owing to the V2+/V3+ redox couple, which corresponded to the two-phase transition between Na3V2(PO4)3 and Na4V2(PO4)3.                         cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene modified sodium vanadium fluorophosphate as a high voltage cathode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ruan, Yan-Li; Wang, Kun; Song, Shi-Dong; Han, Xu; Cheng, Bo-Wen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Substantial interests have been paid to Na-based electrode materials due to the abundance and low cost of sodium resources on earth.  In this study, we improved the electrochem. performance of NaVPO4F cathode by coating graphene sheets.  The structure, compn. and morphol. of NaVPO4F/graphene composite were investigated by x-ray diffraction, FTIR, FE-SEM and TEM.  FE-SEM and TEM anal. indicate that the graphene sheets were successfully coated on the surface of NaVPO4F. After 50 charge/discharge cycles at 0.05C, the capacity retention of the cathode could reach up to 97.7%.  Although the discharge capacity of NaVPO4F/graphene decreased to 70.1 mA-h/g under a high rate of 0.5C, it returned back to 113.2 mA-h/g once the rate was reduced to 0.05C.  Electrochem. impedance spectroscopy measurement further reveals that the NaVPO4F/graphene electrode exhibited a faster sodium-ion diffusivity and less resistance compared with the pure NaVPO4F.                         cas_cit62R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">62</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sn-Doped V2O5 Film with Enhanced Lithium-Ion Storage Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yanwei; Yao, Jinhuan; Uchaker, Evan; Zhang, Ming; Tian, Jianjun; Liu, Xiaoyan; Cao, Guozhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>

                        cas_cit65R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">65</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin Oxide/Graphene Aerogel Nanocomposites Building Superior Rate Capability for Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fan, Linlin; Li, Xifei; Cui, Yanhua; Xu, Hui; Zhang, Xianfa; Xiong, Dongbin; Yan, Bo; Wang, Yufen; Li, Dejun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">176</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">610-619</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">SnO2 has attracted intense interest for use as an anode material for Li-ion batteries because of various advantages of the high theor. capacity and low-cost.  Unfortunately, SnO2 anode material suffers from the huge vol. change and poor elec. cond.  To address these problems, SnO2/graphene aerogel composites have been successfully synthesized by a facile hydrothermal approach. 3-4 nm-sized SnO2 nanoparticles are uniformly dispersed over graphene aerogels.  The hydrothermal reaction time highly affects the electrode performance of the anodes.  The nanocomposite electrode with reaction time of 3 h shows increased electrochem. performance with high energy capacity, long cycle life, and superior rate capability.  After 100 cycles, it can deliver a high discharge capacity of 662 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1.  At 500 mA g-1, it can still yield a discharge capacity of 619.7 mA h g-1 after 723 cycles.  The performance improvement can attribute to the graphene aerogel, which can suppress the aggregation of SnO2 nanoparticles, enhance the cond. of SnO2, and increase their structural stability during cycling.  The SnO2/graphene aerogel composite is a promising anode material building high performance Li ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpwDhKuOg_8a7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lglK39M7gaOUA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVajtbvF&amp;md5=503fbac3017ba8f37f9b4e7905170841</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref66"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref66'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">66</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit66" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2017.03.183"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yin, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chai, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kong, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Preparation of Hierarchical SnS<sub>2</sub>/SnO<sub>2</sub> Anode with Enhanced Electrochemical Performances for Lithium-ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         cas_cit66R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">66</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Preparation of hierarchical SnS2/SnO2 anode with enhanced electrochemical performances for lithium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Lixiong; Chai, Simin; Huang, Jianfeng; Kong, Xingang; Pan, Limin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">238</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
