        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hierarchical SnS2/SnO2 composites were successfully synthesized by a facile 1-step solvothermal method.  The basic nature of the soln. plays a crucial role in ascertaining the phase and structures of the Sn-based products.  And compared with plate-like SnS2 nanoparticles fabricated in deionized H2O (DI w), the sphere-like SnS2/SnO2 composites obtained in anhyd. EtOH (AE) exhibit excellent electrochem. performances as anode material for Li-ion batteries (LIBs).  The discharge capacity of SnS2/SnO2 electrode retains 588.15 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 50 cycles, and the discharge capacity of the electrode can still stably reserve 559.16 mA h g-1 even at 800 mA g-1, demonstrating a significantly increased cycling reversibility and structural stability compared to the bare SnS2.  The sphere-like SnS2/SnO2 structure are assembled by nanoparticles, which can shorten the Li-ions/electrons pathways, the hierarchical structure of SnS2/SnO2 composites can accommodate the large vol. variation.  The charge/discharge performance of the SnS2/SnO2 composites can also be enhanced by the synergy effects of SnS2 and SnO2.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGohPGgO0aMXzbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lglK39M7gaOUA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXmvFWhu7s%253D&amp;md5=17345754ff72902529451f6302c4f390</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref67"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref67'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">67</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit67" data-doi="10.1039/C3EE42704H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Banis, M. N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lushington, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cai, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Atomic Layer Deposition of Solid-state Electrolyte Coated Cathode Materials with Superior High-voltage Cycling Behavior for Lithium Ion Battery Application</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ. Sci.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">7</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">768</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">778</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C3EE42704H</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D7%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D768-778%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26author%3DX.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BLiu%26author%3DM.%2BN.%2BBanis%26author%3DA.%2BLushington%26author%3DR.%2BLi%26author%3DM.%2BCai%26author%3DX.%2BSun%26title%3DAtomic%2BLayer%2BDeposition%2Bof%2BSolid-state%2BElectrolyte%2BCoated%2BCathode%2BMaterials%2Bwith%2BSuperior%2BHigh-voltage%2BCycling%2BBehavior%2Bfor%2BLithium%2BIon%2BBattery%2BApplication%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC3EE42704H&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b18195&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC3EE42704H&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit67R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">67</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atomic layer deposition of solid-state electrolyte coated cathode materials with superior high-voltage cycling behavior for lithium ion battery application</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Xifei; Liu, Jian; Banis, Mohammad Norouzi; Lushington, Andrew; Li, Ruying; Cai, Mei; Sun, Xueliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">768-778</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">LiNi1/3Co1/3Mn1/3O2 (NMC) is a highly promising cathode material for use in lithium ion batteries; unfortunately, its poor cycling performance at high cutoff voltages hinders its commercialization.  In this study, for the first time, we employ at. layer deposition (ALD) to coat lithium tantalum oxide, a solid-state electrolyte, with varying thicknesses on NMC in an attempt to improve battery performance.  Our results indicate that utilization of a solid-state electrolyte as a coating material for NMC significantly improves performance at high cutoff voltages but is strongly dependent on coating thicknesses.  Our investigation revealed that a thicker coating proved to be beneficial in preventing cathode material dissoln. into the electrolyte and aided in maintaining the microstructure of NMC.  Consequently, a thicker ALD coating resulted in increased electrochem. impedance of the cathode.  The results of this study indicate that an optimized coating thickness is needed in order to strike a balance between maintaining structural stability while minimizing electrochem. impedance.  The coating thicknesses are functionally specific, and for the best improvement of a cathode, a particular coating thickness should be sought.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr432_eespCI7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lglK39M7gaOUA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhsFaksLc%253D&amp;md5=a4fb112025ec7d2324d0a78011c39ae9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref68"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref68'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">68</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit68" data-doi="10.1016/j.jtice.2016.07.003"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, C. J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tseng, C. M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chang, J. K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, T. C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structure-mediated Electrochemical Performance of SnS<sub>2</sub> Anode for Li-ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Taiwan Inst. Chem. Eng.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">66</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">292</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">300</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jtice.2016.07.003</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D66%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D292-300%26journal%3DJ.%2BTaiwan%2BInst.%2BChem.%2BEng.%26author%3DK.%2BWu%26author%3DC.%2BJ.%2BWu%26author%3DC.%2BM.%2BTseng%26author%3DJ.%2BK.%2BChang%26author%3DT.%2BC.%2BLee%26title%3DStructure-mediated%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BSnS2%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BLi-ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jtice.2016.07.003&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b18195&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jtice.2016.07.003&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit68R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">68</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structure-mediated electrochemical performance of SnS2 anode for Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Karen; Wu, Chia-Jung; Tseng, Chuan-Ming; Chang, Jeng-Kuei; Lee, Tai-Chou</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Taiwan Institute of Chemical Engineers</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">66</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">292-300</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JTICA8</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1876-1070</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, SnS2 powders with various surface morphologies are prepd. using a facile solvothermal route with three different solvents.  The powders synthesized in ethylene glycol and deionized water exhibit aggregates composed of nanoplates, whereas those synthesized in ethanol show flower-like microspheres (diam.: 1-2 μm) composed of nanosheets (thickness: 60-70 nm).  The hierarchical flower-like microstructures can alleviate the vol. change during charge/discharge cycles due to their porous nature.  In addn., SnS2 synthesized at a lower temp. (100 °C) has nanoplates with a lower thickness, improving electrochem. performance.  At a const. c.d. of 300 mA g-1, the microflowers exhibit a reversible capacity of 460 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles, a retention of 84%.  More importantly, at a higher c.d. of 5000 mA g-1, a reversible capacity of 285 mAh g-1 is obtained.  This study demonstrates that SnS2 synthesized using suitable processing design strategies can be used as an efficient active material for lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoGruqV-KZIN7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lglK39M7gaOUA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1Sht7fO&amp;md5=096234bc3a70945c5e2eb2a7633d0674</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref69"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref69'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">69</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit69" data-doi="10.1021/acs.jpcc.5b00890"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H. L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, B. J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lei, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Z. Q.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoS<sub>2</sub>/Graphene Hybrid Nanoflowers with Enhanced Electrochemical Performances as Anode for Lithium-ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Phys. Chem. C</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">119</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">7959</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">7968</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.jpcc.5b00890</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D119%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D7959-7968%26journal%3DJ.%2BPhys.%2BChem.%2BC%26author%3DH.%2BL.%2BLi%26author%3DK.%2BYu%26author%3DH.%2BFu%26author%3DB.%2BJ.%2BGuo%26author%3DX.%2BLei%26author%3DZ.%2BQ.%2BZhu%26title%3DMoS2%252FGraphene%2BHybrid%2BNanoflowers%2Bwith%2BEnhanced%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformances%2Bas%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BLithium-ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.jpcc.5b00890&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b18195&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.jpcc.5b00890&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit69R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">69</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2/Graphene Hybrid Nanoflowers with Enhanced Electrochemical Performances as Anode for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Honglin; Yu, Ke; Fu, Hao; Guo, Bangjun; Lei, Xiang; Zhu, Ziqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">119</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7959-7968</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1932-7447</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, we studied the synthesis and electrochem. performance of MoS2 and reduced graphene oxide (rGO) hybrid nanoflowers for use as anode material in lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  The morphol. and microstructure of the samples were characterized by field emission SEM (FESEM), transmission electron microscopy (TEM), X-ray diffraction (XRD), and X-ray photoelectron spectrometry (XPS).  Herein, the composite nanoflowers delivered a significant enhanced reversible specific capacity and charge/discharge cycle stabilities as anode in comparison with pristine MoS2.  Electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS) measurements indicated that the incorporation of rGO significantly reduced the contact resistance and the improved electrochem. performances could be attributed to the synergy effect between the functions of MoS2 and rGO.  A high reversible capacity of 1150 mAh/g at a current of 0.1 A/g could be retained without fading after 60 cycles.  The rate performance of the composite was also improved, and the specific capacity remained at the relative high value of ∼890 mAh/g even at a current of 1 A/g.  To further systematically study the mechanism of the improved LIBs performances for composite, we constructed the corresponding models based on expt. data and conducted a first-principles calcn.  The nudged elastic band (NEB) method was employed to study the diffusion of Li in different structures.  The calcd. results proved that the diffusion barrier for Li in MoS2/graphene was significantly lower than that in pristine MoS2 and presented a theor. explanation for a better diffusivity property.  The high specific capacity and excellent cycling stability of these hybrid nanoflowers are competent as a promising anode material for high-performance LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a             }
        }, 100);
    });
    </script>

                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbonized-leaf Membrane with Anisotropic Surfaces for Sodium-ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Hongbian; Shen, Fei; Luo, Wei; Dai, Jiaqi; Han, Xiaogang; Chen, Yanan; Yao, Yonggang; Zhu, Hongli; Fu, Kun; Hitz, Emily; Hu, Liangbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2204-2210</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A simple one-step thermal pyrolysis route has been developed to prep. carbon membrane from a natural leaf.  The carbonized leaf membrane possesses anisotropic surfaces and internal hierarchical porosity, exhibiting a high specific capacity of 360 mAh/g and a high initial Coulombic efficiency of 74.8% as a binder-free, current-collector-free anode for rechargeable sodium ion batteries.  Moreover, large-area carbon membranes with low contact resistance are fabricated by simply stacking and carbonizing leaves, a promising strategy toward large-scale sodium-ion battery developments.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqpldZ4FmRhnrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9DiYvwhnrjg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xis1Kmuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=24f3d46a90c1c53822a21989b6b9caab</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2017.02.200"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shen, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemical Study of Na<sub>0.66</sub>Ni<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67–x</sub>Mo<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> as Cathode Material for Sodium-ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Alloys Compd.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">709</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">481</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">486</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jallcom.2017.02.200</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical study of Na0.66Ni0.33Mn0.67-xMoxO2 as cathode material for sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Jiale; Shen, Jianxing; Wang, Tailin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">709</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">481-486</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JALCEU</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0925-8388</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">P2-type Na0.66Ni0.33Mn0.67-xMoxO2 (x = 0, 0.03, 0.05, 0.07) were prepd. using a conventional solid state method and for the 1st time developed as promising cathode materials for Na-ion batteries.  The XRD patterns show that Mo6+ ions are successfully incorporated into the lattice of the Na-Ni-Mn-O system and the P2-type structure remains unchanged after substitution.  The introduction of Mo6+ in the Na-Ni-Mn-O system can improve capacity retention compared to the unsubstituted material during cycling.  An addnl. charge/discharge profile can be obsd. between 3.0 and 3.2 V for Mo-substituted samples, demonstrating that Na+/vacancy ordering can be suppressed during Na insertion/extn.  Na0.66Ni0.33Mn0.62Mo0.05O2 can deliver an initial capacity of 112 mA-h/g at 34 mA g-1 with a high av. voltage of 3.6 V and a capacity retention of 87% after 50 cycles.  EIS measurements demonstrate that Mo-substitution is an effective way to hinder the increase of inter-particle contact resistance by suppressing any possible irreversible phase transformation found at low Na contents.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpNDmDAENJYIbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgSPMOtmM2rug"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvFeisr0%253D&amp;md5=0a0c3d54f2a202da1fe5f2f4237b013c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201703086"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jin, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiao, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">1D Nanomaterials: Design, Synthesis, and Applications in Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Small</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1703086</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have emerged in recent years, due to their advantages of natural abundance, low cost and environmental friendliness.  In this article, we review the up-to-date research progress on anode materials for Na-ion batteries from five respects: carbon-based materials, alloy-based materials, metal oxides and sulfides based on conversion reaction, titanium-based compds. with insertion mechanism, and org. composites.  In particular, we not only summarize the Na-storage mechanism of these anodes, but also discuss the failure mechanism.  The problems and challenges assocd. with these anodes are pointed out.  Furthermore, on the basis of extensive reports and our exptl. studies, feasible strategies are suggested for designing high performance anode materials.  After further in-depth exploration and investigation, we believe that Na-ion batteries are promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries for low cost and large-scale energy storage systems in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrB4Pf2vZ5QrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgSPMOtmM2rug"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFelsrnN&amp;md5=8311789a2dc4e61dabff177245235c3e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.matlet.2015.05.041"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bao, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhong, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhan, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">One-pot Synthesis of FeF<sub>3</sub>/Graphene Composite for Sodium Secondary Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Mater.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The microstructural changes and phase transformations of tin nanoparticles during electrochem. sodiation were studied with a nanosized sodium ion battery using in situ TEM.  The first sodiation process occurred in two steps; i.e., the cryst. Sn nanoparticles were initially sodiated via a two-phase mechanism with a migrating phase boundary to form a Na-poor, amorphous NaxSn alloy (x ∼ 0.5), which was further sodiated to several Na-rich amorphous phases and finally to the crystd.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultrafine SnS2 nanocrystals-reduced graphene oxide nanoribbon paper (SnS2-RGONRP) was created by a well-designed process including in situ redn., evapn.-induced self-assembly, and sulfuration.  The as-formed SnS2 nanocrystals possess an av. diam. of 2.3 nm and disperse on the surface of RGONRs uniformly.  The strong capillary force formed during evapn. leads to a compact assembly of RGONRs to give a flexible paper structure with a high d. of 0.94 g/cm3.  The as-prepd. SnS2-RGONRP composite could be directly used as free-standing electrode for Na ion batteries.  Due to the synergistic effects between the ultrafine SnS2 nanocrystals and the conductive, tightly connected RGONR networks, the composite paper electrode exhibits excellent electrochem. performance.  A high volumetric capacity of 508-244 mAh/cm3 was obtained at current densities of 0.1-10 A/g.  Discharge capacities of 334 and 255 mAh/cm3 were still kept, even after 1500 cycles tested at current densities of 1 and 5 A/g, resp.  This strategy provides insight into a new pathway for the creation of free-standing composite electrodes used in the energy storage and conversion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoCYhQE_YL7F7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgdDUgwpSYjFQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXmsFWku7Y%253D&amp;md5=75201ed26dc4be08a6c0cdb3ad070998</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref10" class="rightTabRefNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit10" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201304962"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Engelhard, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Non-lithium metals such as Na have attracted attention as a potential charge carrying ion for rechargeable batteries.  Using in situ TEM in combination with d. functional theory calcns., the authors probed the structural and chem. evolution of SnO2 nanowire anodes in Na-ion batteries and compared them quant. with results from Li-ion batteries.  Upon Na insertion into SnO2, a displacement reaction occurs, giving amorphous NaxSn nanoparticles dispersed in Na2O matrix.  With further Na insertion, the NaxSn crystd. into Na15Sn4 (x = 3.75).  Upon extn. of Na (de-sodiation), the NaxSn transforms to Sn nanoparticles.  Assocd. with the de-alloying, pores form, leading to a structure of Sn particles confined in a hollow matrix of Na2O.  These pores greatly increase elec. impedance, therefore accounting for the poor cyclability of SnO2.  DFT calcns. indicate that Na+ diffuses 30 times slower than Li+ in SnO2, in agreement with in situ TEM measurement.  Insertion of Na can chemomechanically soften the reaction product to a greater extent than in lithiation.  Therefore, in contrast to the lithiation of SnO2 significantly less dislocation plasticity was seen ahead of the sodiation front.  This direct comparison of the results from Na and Li highlights the crit. role of ionic size and electronic structure of different ionic species on the charge/discharge rate and failure mechanisms in these batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrxbnVD4FT9W7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgdDUgwpSYjFQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsFels7zP&amp;md5=3eeb24d9885b1c825918e689b7adbbb2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-014-0506-z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Seng, K.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The development of materials with unique nanostructures is an effective strategy for the improvement of sodium storage in sodium ion batteries to achieve stable cycling performance and good rate capability.  In this work, SnSb core/carbon-shell nanocables directly anchored on graphene sheets (GS) were synthesized by the hydrothermal technique and chem. vapor deposition.  The simultaneous carbon coating and the encapsulation of SnSb alloy is effective for alleviating the vol.-change problem in sodium ion batteries.  After optimizing the electrolyte for SnSb in the sodium ion batteries, the optimized coaxial SnSb/carbon nanocable/GS (SnSb/CNT@GS) nanostructure demonstrated stable cycling capability and rate performance in 1 M NaClO4 with propylene carbonate (PC) + 5% fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC).  The SnSb/CNT@GS electrode can retain a capacity of 360 mAh/g for up to 100 cycles, which is 71% of the theor. capacity.  This is higher than in the other three electrolytes tested (1 M NaClO4 in PC, 1 M NaClO4 in PC/FEC (1:1 vol./vol.) and 1 M NaPF6 + PC), and higher than that of the sample without the addn. of graphene.  The good electrochem. performance can be attributed to the efficient buffering provided by the outer carbon nanocable layer and the graphene inhibiting the agglomeration of SnSb particles, as well as its high cond.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpxy6wY3P3PGrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgdDUgwpSYjFQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtlKht7nF&amp;md5=831cecb3ad9e9fd6b40bfcb18ffc4a15</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref13" class="rightTabRefNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit13" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA01963J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jahel, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ghimbeu, C.                         rightTab-cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exceptionally highly performing Na-ion battery anode using crystalline SnO2 nanoparticles confined in mesoporous carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jahel, Ali; Ghimbeu, Camelia Matei; Darwiche, Ali; Vidal, Loic; Hajjar-Garreau, Samar; Vix-Guterl, Cathie; Monconduit, Laure</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Confined and unconfined SnO2 nanoparticles in the pores of mesoporous carbon were prepd. and tested as anode materials vs. Na.  Both composites present small cryst. SnO2 particles (∼3 nm) but different location and dispersion in the carbon matrix.  When the particles are homogeneously distributed and confined in the carbon pores, an initial reversible capacity of 780 mA h g-1 is achieved with unprecedented capacity retention of 80 and 54% after 100 and 4000 cycles, resp., at a high current rate (50 C, 1800 mA g-1).  Unexpectedly, over two current rate variation cycles from 1 C to 500 C, the composite recovers 81% and 97%, resp. after returning from the 500 C to the 1 C rate.  To our knowledge, no other material with such a long cycling life and superior performance in terms of capacity and rate capability has been reported so far for sodium ion batteries.  HRTEM, XRD, N2 adsorption, XPS and galvanostatic cycling results suggest that confined SnO2 particles undergo an enhanced sodium alloying/dealloying process due to their special confinement inside the pores, which increases their cond., facilitates the diffusion of Na+ ions and buffers the large volumetric changes during charge/discharge.  These high performances cannot be delivered when SnO2 is not confined and not well dispersed in the carbon pores.  This work demonstrates that nano-confinement of anode species in carbon is a valuable concept affording the modification of the fundamental properties of guest species along with their electrochem. performances leading to highly stable and performing materials with a long life for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpmSgtWPTSt8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgdDUgwpSYjFQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXnsFGgur4%253D&amp;md5=219ee2777f1e53956a82fdbab173128f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201502057"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Feng, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiong, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lawes, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Controlled SnO<sub>2</sub> Crystallinity Effectively Dominating Sodium Storage Performance</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion Battery is attractive alternative to Li-ion battery due to the natural abundance of Na resource. In this review, we summarize the up-to-date progress on the rational design and efficient synthesis of MSs with controlled morphologies, sizes, compns., and micro/nano-structures, along with their applications as electrode materials for lithium/sodium/magnesium-ion batteries and supercapacitors, and electrocatalysts for the oxygen redn. reaction and the hydrogen evolution reaction.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Binders play a significant role in enhancing the electrochem. performance of tin disulfide (SnS2) as the anode for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) because of their excellent dispersion and cohesion in the electrodes. When sodium alginate (SA), CM-cellulose (CMC), poly acrylic acid (PAA), and CMC-PAA (1:1, wt%) are applied as binders for the SnS2 anode electrode (the obtained electrodes are denoted as SnS2-S, SnS2-C, SnS2-CP, and SnS2-P, resp.) in LIBs, the electrodes exhibited high reversible lithium-ion storage capacities of 762.00 mA h g-1, 891.65 mA h g-1, 913.94 mA h g-1, and 930.36 mA h g-1 at the current densities of 100 mA g-1, resp.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A hybrid structure involving efficient plentiful ultrasmall SnS2 nanocrystals decorated on flexible reduced graphene oxide (RGO) has been successfully realized via a simple refluxing method.  Compared to previous studies, the ultrasmall SnS2 nanocrystals can compactly and orderly cover the RGO nanosheets, increasing the loading no. of SnS2 per unit area of the RGO substrates.  The ultrasmall SnS2 nanocrystals@RGO nanocomposites were investigated as electrode materials for lithium-ion batteries.  In this hybrid structure, RGO was not only used as a solid support to uniformly distribute the SnS2 nanocrystals, but also as a carrier to accelerate electron transport.  In addn., the uniform size and homogeneous SnS2 nanocrystals on the RGO nanosheets reduced electrode polarization, resulting in excellent electrochem. performance for lithium-ion batteries.  A specific capacity up to 1034 mA-h/g was realized from an ultrasmall SnS2 nanocrystals@RGO electrode even after 200 cycles at 0.1C.  Importantly, the ultrasmall SnS2 nanocrystals@RGO electrode showed excellent capacity retention for up to 450 cycles even at a high rate of 5C.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have been considered as promising alternatives to Li-ion batteries due to the natural abundance of sodium resources.  Searching for high-performance anode materials currently becomes a hot topic and also a great challenge for developing Na-ion batteries.  In this work, a novel hybrid anode is synthesized consisting of ultrafine, few-layered SnS2 anchored on few-layered reduced graphene oxide (rGO) by a facile solvothermal route.  The SnS2/rGO hybrid exhibits a high capacity, ultralong cycle life, and superior rate capability.  The hybrid can deliver a high charge capacity of 649 mA-h/g at 100 mA/g.  At 800 mA/g (1.8C), it can yield an initial charge capacity of 469 mA-h/g, which can be maintained at 89% and 61%, resp., after 400 and 1000 cycles.  The hybrid can also sustain a c.d. up to 12.8 A/g (≈28C) where the charge process can be completed in only 1.3 min while still delivering a charge capacity of 337 mA-h/g.  The fast and stable Na-storage ability of SnS2/rGO makes it a promising anode for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2sS3KKxaUkbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-5BMeZKKpgA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvF2ms7jI&amp;md5=173a3c027a58922c59d5633c7a05d580</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref23" class="rightTabRefNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit23" data-doi="10.1039/C4NR05106H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Exfoliated-SnS(2) Restacked on Graphene as a High-capacity, High-rate, and Long-cycle Life Anode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">7</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1325</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1332</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exfoliated-SnS2 restacked on graphene as a high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Kang, Hongyan; Jiao, Lifang; Chen, Chengcheng; Cao, Kangzhe; Wang, Yijing; Yuan, Huatang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1325-1332</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Designed as a high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life anode for sodium ion batteries, exfoliated-SnS2 restacked on graphene is prepd. by the hydrolysis of lithiated SnS2 followed by a facile hydrothermal method.  Structural and morphol. characterizations demonstrate that ultrasmall SnS2 nanoplates (with a typical size of 20-50 nm) composed of 2-5 layers are homogeneously decorated on the surface of graphene, while the hybrid structure self-assembles into a three-dimensional (3D) network architecture.  The obtained SnS2/graphene nanocomposite delivers a remarkable capacity as high as 650 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1.  More impressively, the capacity can reach 326 mA h g-1 even at 4000 mA g-1 and remains stable at ∼610 mA h g-1 without fading up to 300 cycles when the rate is brought back to 200 mA g-1.  The excellent electrochem. performance is attributed to the synergetic effects between the ultrasmall SnS2 and the highly conductive graphene network.  The unique structure can simultaneously facilitate Na+ ion diffusion, provide more reaction sites, and suppress aggregation and vol. fluctuation of the active materials during prolonged cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRwuFHeQ2-ZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-5BMeZKKpgA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhslelt7fN&amp;md5=8bd01685b22c4afe0f313378ef72187b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.1039/c2cp40790f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xin, H.                         rightTab-cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Doping carbons beyond nitrogen: an overview of advanced heteroatom doped carbons with boron, sulphur and phosphorus for energy applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Paraknowitsch, Jens Peter; Thomas, Arne</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),

        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Heteroatom doped carbon materials represent one of the most prominent families of materials that are used in energy related applications, such as fuel cells, batteries, hydrogen storage or supercapacitors.  While doping carbons with nitrogen atoms has experienced great progress throughout the past decades and yielded promising material concepts, also other doping candidates have gained the researchers' interest in the last few years.  Boron is already relatively widely studied, and as its electronic situation is contrary to the one of nitrogen, codoping carbons with both heteroatoms can probably create synergistic effects.  Sulfur and phosphorus have just recently entered the world of carbon synthesis, but already the first studies published prove their potential, esp. as electrocatalysts in the cathodic compartment of fuel cells.  Due to their size and their electronegativity being lower than those of carbon, structural distortions and changes of the charge densities are induced in the carbon materials.  This article is to give a state of the art update on the most recent developments concerning the advanced heteroatom doping of carbon that goes beyond nitrogen.  Doped carbon materials and their applications in energy devices are discussed with respect to their boron-, sulfur- and phosphorus-doping.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrXYE3FbkNibrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-5BMeZKKpgA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsV2it7fO&amp;md5=182291f9157be822fc6701fac47f4c00</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref26" class="rightTabRefNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit26" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201405370"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wickramaratne, N.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Scrupulous design and fabrication of advanced anode materials are of great importance for developing high-performance lithium ion batteries.  Herein, we report a facile strategy for construction of free-standing and free-binder 3D porous carbon coated MoS2/nitrogen-doped graphene (C-MoS2/N-G) integrated electrode via a hydrothermal-induced self-assembly process. As an anode for lithium ion batteries, the C-MoS2/N-G electrode delivers a high first discharge capacity of 1600 mAh g-1 and maintains 900 mAh g-1 after 500 cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Novel N and S dual-doped graphene sheets were synthesized via carbonization of poly(2,5-dimercapto-1,3,4-thiadiazole) (PDMcT) functionalized graphene oxides.  Here, PDMcT, polymd. by the com. available 2,5-dimercapto-1,3,4-thiadiazole (DMcT) monomer is chosen as the N and S precursor, which plays a key role in the formation of N and S dual-doped graphene.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">S/N dual-doped graphene aerogels (SNGAs) with a unique porous network structure were designed through a facile and versatile 1-pot hydrothermal strategy.  When employed as anode in LIBs, the SNGAs with N content of 1.50% and S content of 15.11% exhibit superior cycle life and rate capability.  For example, a high reversible capacity of 1109.8 mAh g-1 can be obtained after 400 cycles even at a high c.d. of 800 mA g-1.  It was discreetly demonstrated that the prominent improved performance of SNGAs can be mainly ascribed to the effect of dual-doping heteroatoms in cooperation with each other in to the graphene lattice as well as the porous nanostructure facilitating the mass transfer for both ions and electrons.  The authors' conclusions illustrate that the strategy of dual-doped graphene aerogel may promote the potential application of graphene for high performance Li ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqx8YbO2cWnRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljY5NnuZcAMhQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XntVGhtro%253D&amp;md5=8a021fd5255ef4127a3b2480786cf9b1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1039/c3nr04823c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lushington, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structurally Tailored Graphene Nanosheets as Lithium Ion Battery Anodes: An Insight to Yield Exceptionally High Lithium Storage Performance</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">12607</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">12615</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">How to tune graphene nanosheets (GNSs) with various morphologies has been a significant challenge for lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  In this study, three types of GNSs with varying size, edge sites, defects and layer nos. have been successfully achieved.  It was demonstrated that controlling GNS morphol. and microstructure has important effects on its cyclic performance and rate capability in LIBs.  Diminished GNS layer no., decreased size, increased edge sites and increased defects in the GNS anode can be highly beneficial to lithium storage and result in increased electrochem. performance.  Interestingly, GNSs treated with a hydrothermal approach delivered a high reversible discharge capacity of 1348 mA h g-1.  This study demonstrates that the controlled design of high performance GNS anodes is an important concept in LIB applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr5ali9odG2K7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljY5NnuZcAMhQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvVejurrE&amp;md5=1d83b24f9f1c1ec31163deddbf6ede55</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref34" class="rightTabRefNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit34" data-doi="10.1021/ja01539a017"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hummers, W.         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">121</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable sodium-ion batteries have lately received considerable attention as an alternative to lithium-ion batteries because sodium resources are essentially inexhaustible and ubiquitous around the world.  Despite recent reports on cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries have shown electrochem. activities close to their lithium-ion counterparts, the major scientific challenge for sodium-ion batteries is to exploit efficient anode materials.  Herein, we demonstrate that a hybrid material composed of few-layer SnS2 nanosheets sandwiched between reduced graphene oxide (RGO) nanosheets exhibits a high specific capacity of 843 mAh/g (calcd. based on the mass of SnS2 only) at a c.d. of 0.1 A/g and a 98% capacity retention after 100 cycles when evaluated between 0.01 and 2.5 V.  Employing ex situ high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy and selected area electron diffraction techniques, we illustrate the high specific capacity of our anode through a 3-fold mechanism of intercalation of sodium ions along the ab-plane of SnS2 nanosheets and the subsequent formation of Na2S2 and Na15Sn4 through conversion and alloy reactions.  The existence of RGO nanosheets in the hybrid material functions as a flexible backbone and high-speed electronic pathways, guaranteeing that an appropriate resilient space buffers the anisotropic dilation of SnS2 nanosheets along the ab-plane and c-axis for stable cycling performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp7u2__bTlgVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhPwNyKgt4rgw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXitVCjtrg%253D&amp;md5=8512fccffb30789680f4d2b2a62843db</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref36" class="rightTabRefNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit36" data-doi="10.1021/am302124f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Preferentialc-axis Orientation of Ultrathin SnS<sub>2</sub> Nanoplates on Graphene as High-performance Anode for Li-ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon nanotubes (CNTs) and nitrogen-doped carbon nanotubes (CNx) were synthesized by the floating catalyst CVD (FCCVD) method. XPS confirms the nitrogen atoms in the graphite matrix and reveals the chem. natures of the doped nitrogen atoms. Pt supported on CNx (Pt/CNx) exhibited a higher electrochem. surface area (ECSA) and higher catalytic activity toward oxygen redn. reaction (ORR), in comparison to Pt supported on CNTs (Pt/CNTs).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Three-dimensional structure-based tin disulfide/vertically aligned carbon nanotube arrays (VACNTs) composites have been successfully fabricated by a facile hydrothermal method for self-assembly with the help of nebulization-assisted infiltration.  The SnS2 particles are anchored on the surface of the VACNTs and the no. of these nanoparticles increases as the nebulization time increase.  The novel three-dimensional structure-based SnS2/VACNTs sample with the SnS2 content of 67 wt.% exhibits excellent electrochem. performance, including high capacity (738 mA-h/g at 50 mA/g after 1st cycle), good cycle stability (551 mA-h/g at 100 mA/g after 100 cycles), and excellent rate capability (223 mA-h/g at 2000 mA/g) when used as an anode in lithium-ion batteries.  The high electrochem. performance can be attributed to the synergistic effect of SnS2 and the unique microstructure of VACNTs, which provide the rapid pathways for ionic and electronic transport ascribing to their well-directed one-dimensional conductive electron paths and well defined regular pore structures.  The VACNTs serve as not only conductive additives to improve the cond. of SnS2 in the composites, but also as buffer matrix to restrain the vol. change of SnS2 and stabilize the electrode structure during the alloying/dealloying process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqOvZz-WSH4CrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhPwNyKgt4rgw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitVakt7nL&amp;md5=0df0414ed7a1fac249de5ea8ec21c1b9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref43" class="rightTabRefNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.03.048"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shen, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In Situ Assembly of Graphene Sheets-supported SnS<sub>2</sub> Nanoplates into 3D Macroporous Aerogels for High-performance Lithium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Three-dimensional (3D) SnS2/graphene aerogels (SnS2/G-As) have been successfully fabricated via an in situ macroscopy self-assembly of graphene sheets which embedded SnS2 nanoplates in a hydrothermal process, and then freeze-drying to maintain the 3D monolithic architectures.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The reversible electrochem. storage of Li+ and Na+ ions is the operating basis of secondary Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  In recent years, there has been rapid growth in the search for appropriate electrode materials.  Nevertheless, the development of host materials for active and durable electrochem. storage of both Li+ and Na+ ions remain challenging.  We report a facile solvothermal method to prep. hierarchical assemblies of thin SnS2 nanosheets in N-methyl-2-pyrrolidone.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The abundance of sodium resources has recently motivated the investigation of sodium ion batteries (SIBs) as an alternative to com. lithium ion batteries.  However, the low power and low capacity of conventional sodium anodes hinder their practical realization.  Although most research has concd. on the development of high-capacity sodium anodes, anodes with a combination of high power and high capacity have not been widely realized.  Herein, we present a simple microwave irradn. technique for obtaining few-layered, ultrathin two-dimensional SnS2 over graphene sheets in a few minutes.  SnS2 possesses a large no. of active surface sites and exhibits high-capacity, rapid sodium ion storage kinetics induced by quick, nondestructive pseudocapacitance.  Enhanced sodium ion storage at a high c.d. (12 A g-1), accompanied by high reversibility and high stability, was demonstrated.  Addnl., a rationally designed sodium ion full cell coupled with SnS2//Na3V2(PO4)3 exhibited exceptional performance with high initial Coulombic efficiency (99%), high capacity, high stability, and a retention of ∼53% of the initial capacity even after the c.d. was increased by a factor of 140.  In addn., a high specific energy of ∼140 Wh kg-1 and an ultrahigh specific power of ∼8.3 kW kg-1 (based on the mass of both the anode and cathode) were obsd.  Because of its outstanding performance and rapid synthesis, few-layered SnS2 could be a promising candidate for practical realization of high-power SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrGRiDOPGxr67Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh2kW4ZEC_eyg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhslags77F&amp;md5=b0d6b6a8322c73803b08e14a8891aae0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref52" class="rightTabRefNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit52" data-doi="10.1039/c3ta15248k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Prikhodchenko, P.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Cost-effective sodium ion batteries (SIBs) are emerging as a desirable alternative choice to lithium ion batteries in terms of application in large-scale energy storage devices.  SnS2 is regarded as a potential anode material for SIBs because of its unique layered structure and high theor. specific capacity.  However, the development of SnS2 was hindered by the sluggish kinetics of the diffusion process and the inevitable vol. change during repeated sodiation- desodiation processes.  In this work, SnS2 with a unique nanowall array (NWA) structure is fabricated by one-step pulsed spray evapn. chem. vapor deposition (PSE-CVD), which could be used directly as binder-free and carbon-free anodes for SIBs.  The SnS2 NWA electrode achieves a high reversible capacity of 576 mAh g-1 at 500 mA g-1 and enhanced cycling stability.  Attractively, an excellent rate capability is demonstrated with ∼370 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1, corresponding to a capacity retention of 64.2% at 500 mA g-1.  The superior sodium storage capability of the SnS2 NWA electrode could be attributed to outstanding electrode design and a rational growth process, which favor fast electron and Na-ion transport, as well as provide steady structure for elongated cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpGXtGr2cKfFrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgeYU59zQA8xQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXht1eiurg%253D&amp;md5=e9231a5ee5bb3602d5873564a8cd8230</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref54" class="rightTabRefNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit54" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b02413"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mao, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gao, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mignerey, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Solid-state Fabrication of SnS<sub>2</sub>/C Nanospheres for High-performance Sodium Ion Battery Anode</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin disulfide (SnS2) has emerged as a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries (NIBs) due to its unique layered structure, high theor. capacity, and low cost.  Conventional SnS2 nanomaterials are normally synthesized using hydrothermal method, which is time-consuming and difficult to scale up for mass prodn.  In this study, we develop a simple solid-state reaction method, in which the carbon-coated SnS2 (SnS2/C) anode materials were synthesized by annealing metallic Sn, sulfur powder, and polyacrylonitrile in a sealed vacuum glass tube.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sn disulfide (SnS2) hierarchical structures were synthesized via a simple hydrothermal route for their use in Li-ion batteries.  The issue of fast capacity degrdn. over cycling because of the dramatic vol. change that causes particle pulverization and poor contact between the active material and current collector is explored and alleviated for the 1st time by surface modification of the whole SnS2 electrode via a facile at. layer deposition (ALD).  ALD allows the uniform formation of conformal Al2O3 coatings onto the porous electrode, and thereby succeeds to enhance their electrochem. performance.  As compared, within fifty battery cycles the bare SnS2 electrode exhibits a final capacity of 219.2 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1, while the coated electrode can deliver the final capacity of 351.1 mA h g-1 (60% larger).  The capacity retention and rate capability of the coated electrode is found much better than that of the bare one.  Electrochem. impedance spectroscopy analyses indicate that the resistance derived from solid-electrolyte interface (SEI) and charge transfer process remains fairly smaller in the coated electrode than in the bare one.  The better electrode kinetics accounts for the strengthened Li-ion intercalation behaviors of the modified electrodes, and demonstrates that ALD oxide coatings are able to enhance the mech. integrity and structural stability of SnS2 electrodes, thus effectively impeding the pulverization of active particles and maintaining good electronic conduction paths and efficient charge transfer.  Also, ALD coatings cover the entire electrode and reduce electrolyte decompn. to attenuate the SEI layer, which also contributes to the cyclability of SnS2.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq6i2Kw6kYT8bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgeYU59zQA8xQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXnslOmsbk%253D&amp;md5=f4407448c59c143fcec4462e76a86414</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref57" class="rightTabRefNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit57" data-doi="10.1021/am200933m"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhai, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Du, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Multiwalled Carbon Nanotubes Anchored with SnS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets as High-performance Anode Materials of Lithium-ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel electrode material for sodium-ion batteries, Na3V2(PO4)3 with a rhombohedral, Na+ superionic conductor (NASICON)-type structure, was synthesized via a solid-state carbothermal redn. reaction assisted by mechanochem. activation.  Electron microscopy anal. showed that the synthesized Na3V2(PO4)3 particles had an av. size of 300 nm, being coated with a uniform layer of carbon 3 nm in thickness.  As a cathode material, Na3V2(PO4)3/C exhibited an initial specific discharge capacity of 98.17 mA-h/g at 0.1C for potentials ranging from 2.5 to 3.8 V.  This was owing to the V3+/V4+ redox couple, which corresponded to the two-phase transition between Na3V2(PO4)3 and NaV2(PO4)3.  The cathode lost 4.92% of its discharge specific capacity after 50 cycles.  As an anode material, Na3V2(PO4)3/C exhibited an initial specific discharge capacity of 63.2 mA-h/g at 0.1C for potentials ranging from 1.0 to 2.5 V.  This was owing to the V2+/V3+ redox couple, which corresponded to the two-phase transition between Na3V2(PO4)3 and Na4V2(PO4)3.  The anode lost approx. 5.41% of its discharge specific capacity after 50 cycles.  The three-dimensional channel structure of NaV2(PO4)3 and the changes induced in its lattice parameters during the charge/discharge processes were simulated on the basis of d. functional theory.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqL5W7t4QuZY7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljAzLNDV42EMQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXps12lsbk%253D&amp;md5=59ad73ad234d3ab597038123cdf3347c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref60"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref60" class="rightTabRefNumLink">60</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit60" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.01.186"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ruan, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Substantial interests have been paid to Na-based electrode materials due to the abundance and low cost of sodium resources on earth.  In this study, we improved the electrochem. performance of NaVPO4F cathode by coating graphene sheets.  The structure, compn. and morphol. of NaVPO4F/graphene composite were investigated by x-ray diffraction, FTIR, FE-SEM and TEM.  FE-SEM and TEM anal. indicate that the graphene sheets were successfully coated on the surface of NaVPO4F.  The NaVPO4F/graphene composite could be operated at a high working potential (3.95 V for av. voltage), and displayed the highest capacity of 120.9 mA-h/g.  After 50 charge/discharge cycles at 0.05C, the capacity retention of the cathode could reach up to 97.7%.  Although the discharge capacity of NaVPO4F/graphene decreased to 70.1 mA-h/g under a high rate of 0.5C, it returned back to 113.2 mA-h/g once the rate was reduced to 0.05C.  Electrochem. impedance spectroscopy measurement further reveals that the NaVPO4F/graphene electrode exhibited a faster sodium-ion diffusivity and less resistance compared with the pure NaVPO4F.  Our results demonstrate that NaVPO4F/graphene is a promising cathode material for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoyYEVnYAgWw7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljAzLNDV42EMQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvFSjtrg%253D&amp;md5=f3ec2d32546b72a0ceb964144fa5897a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref61" class="rightTabRefNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit61" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.04.094"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Serras, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Palomares, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Goñi, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kubiak, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rojo, T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemical Performance of Mixed Valence Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2x</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3–2x</sub>/C as Cathode for Sodium-ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.
